puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large amount of decayed matter in it, and it comes up to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	one must scrape and cover all of it up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in a man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and assistance from it in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matter came to the leg, and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to pierce it to open it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctor through his folly operated so much that the abscess opened,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and much matter came out of it, and it became a fistula, and there were many wounds that all bled and discharged moisture from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many put off treatment for around two years, and no one had any skill in the art of medicine,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called there, and saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and that which flowed from the holes in great quantity;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and became red the body of the young man, and had a yellow colour.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I pitched a tent at one of these holes, and then searched all the holes,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came across from others in all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	So I hurried and dug into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it rotten and pierced, with corruption coming up to the bone inside;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I saw what appeared to be rotten bone, and I thought there was no other corruption except that which I removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	And I began to heal the wound with hot medicine for a long time, but it would not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then I began again, and uncovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and found that the corruption was continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then tried to heal the wound;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not until I cut around a palm's width of bone, and the pain left completely.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	Then I treated it with medicine; and he was healed and sewn up quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and the operation did not need to be repeated except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure it,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of my fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	Because through the evacuation of blood he often bled, but he was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there grew a hard lump in the place of the bone, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or discomfort anywhere, neither when walking nor standing.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in the following manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a ligature and tie it tightly around the head of the bone that protrudes,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and instruct someone to hold it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another larger piece of linen on top of the first bandage, and tie it over the flesh that is above the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and hold the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh towards the bottom,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh above the place where you want to cut, so that the blade doesn't cut into the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot brand or a flat object under the bone to cover the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and one must work as long as possible until one can see and smell the corruption, then stop.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is rotten and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	cut away all the flesh; then place a hot brand under it,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then bring the two parts of the broken bone together, and let the healing take place from the end of the break, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the joint, and let the bone where it is corrupted heal from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there is no need to cut, except for the corruption itself;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is at the base of the hand or the foot, and it is very serious,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but you should still examine this erosion, how it appeared to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in every way you can, but be careful not to damage the vein or nerve;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the knives and probes for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of the joints,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, one must prepare an instrument for each type of procedure.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And you should know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need according to your knowledge of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of the illnesses;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you consider the instrument which you need according to what is appropriate for it.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulders may dislocate due to internal causes or external forces.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have applied that corrosion through the cure of medicines, and it does not help,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then you must treat the shoulder joint; it is necessary to cover that member up to the point where the corrosion occurs,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient escapes through the sky from death, or through malice, which is greater, because of the fault in the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so it seems to be burned by fire,
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and after the darkness comes the corrosion of the limb from one member to another,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and affects throughout the body; so you rush to the head,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is through the sting of some venomous beasts, such as the sea scorpion and adder and similar,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the bite is on the head or neck, then cut it, and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches the hand, cut at the joint so that the sting does not go into the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is fatal,
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and it is not appropriate to reduce them below a certain amount due to its virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and thus one proceeds when the erosion occurs in the foot: if it occurs in the first joint, then one treats the next joint afterwards;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it occurs in the foot, then one treats the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, then one treats at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but to kill the patient.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way to cover the limb with a cloth or bandage is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend one minister's hand down from the lower ligature, and another minister's hand up from the upper ligature,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you loosen the skin between the two ligatures to one and a half spans wide, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then the cautery or silk, and place a linen drape on each side so that the silk does not touch the healthy skin
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and bring another injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding occurs when you operate, then cauterize the wound gently,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you can apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the wounded member with a suitable bandage and treat it until it heals.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in a dream:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a darkness that looked like a burn from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this corrosion started first on his toe of the foot, so much that it discolored all the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he stopped covering his feet, and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long after that, the corrosion returned to his finger, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I applied striking remedies after purification of the body, but he could not stop the corrosions;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cover his hand, but I did not want to because I had no hope of striking the matter;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was feeble; and he despaired entirely, and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and cut off his hand, and was healed;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have never heard of anyone doing otherwise if they had need of it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess occurs in a fleshy place, and remains so long that it causes a great gathering of pus;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and drains, and the place remains hollow, just like a vessel;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin above is as thin as a delicate cloth,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not heal up to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "sore",
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called a "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it reaches the bone in an open wound, then it is called a "fistula".;
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is to cover the entire sore, especially when it is thin, just like a cloth.;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	And do not fear for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have confidence that the skin is burning, and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it thus with a clyster:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	observe whether the breasts are large and the pus in them has an evil-smelling odour,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then cleanse with an Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take ashes, and oil, and litharge, equally, and put to cook in .i. vessel over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take some of this according to your need, and make it into water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and enema the breast, and constrict the orifice;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine on for two hours, then remove it by squeezing;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this as many times as necessary, until the breasts are deflated and the pain is relieved;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes they are enema with ashes water,
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you burn vine wood ashes, and pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and enema until you know that the breast is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither Egyptian medicine nor ashes water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then enema with water and honey in which there is a little litharge powder;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you can enema with honey and sweet wine, so that the honey has the property of cleaning and washing,
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and wine makes blood flow;
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and are confident that the wound is clean,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if it cleanses by causing a bowel movement,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and you press out the pus with a syringe, and they treat it with a poultice made of rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or you cleanse it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken in the section on ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the breast is small and the catheter cannot enter,

et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the hole that drips downward is on top, then cut above or below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is perforated, it doesn't allow food to pass through;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound below as you wish,

car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	and when the bowels are empty, they should not be constipated.

pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply ointment to another cloth according to the amount of discharge from the nipple,

Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if milk flows from the breasts for many days, know that the breast is not averted.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom flows after a long time, do not despair of health,

si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the fingernail of the hand, caused by a wound or injury. It can also occur on the toe, although this is less common. The condition is characterized by inflammation and the formation of pus beneath the nail, which can cause discomfort and even pain. In some cases, the nail may separate from the nail bed, allowing for the accumulation of pus underneath. Treatment typically involves draining the abscess to relieve pressure and promote healing. It's important to address panarice promptly to prevent further complications.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or from an injury to the foot, or perhaps it arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then a large abscess develops,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and run and flow low until they reach the root of the nail, and perhaps they will reach all the way.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and the corrosion reaches to the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the shoulder is twice as large, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have described in the section, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	you must cut away all the surplus growth from the nail,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses on the flesh and starts to grow out, and the bleedings
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	you should put the thread under the nail so that it doesn't press against the flesh,

et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on top of the remaining skin burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corrosion is in the bone, then strike it and draw it out, for as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decay, cut it with a chisel as mentioned earlier,

et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is decayed, and hollow, and it hurts a lot, then you must heal it first;

et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and ensure that the incision does not go all the way to the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	if it happens, put something on top of it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the shoulder
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The joints of some people's hands by chance are all fleshy,
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and sometimes there is bone where there should be flesh, and occasionally there is bone where there should be nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and sometimes they grow from the root of the joint, or from the knuckles on the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that grow from the knuckle of the finger do not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that grow from the joint of the finger sometimes move;

En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born in the rectum, it is necessary for you to first cup the fleshy part roundly up to the bone,

Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come by birth, or by wound, or by burn, or similar things.

Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes to one of his hands with the palm, then sew up that wound as it should be.
Des vils	Of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Wounds are large, wrapped, and full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more occurs in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him some purgative medicine, and then the basil oil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is in two ways: one is where you make incisions and draw out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you open a vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The surgery is performed as follows: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the veins are dilated.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then hold the leg from above the thigh down to just below the knee;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then open a vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide cut,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then squeeze and draw out the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood has come out as the patient can tolerate;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then the scurvy, and he is ordered to eat meat seasoned with black holly;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the bloodletting and bleeding when the veins are full, which helps the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The raising of the limb is as follows: lift the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then place it in hot water, and raise the leg until it turns red, and open the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have any bandages, heat them in the fire and then apply them to the vein from above on the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the joint, and scorch the vein on both sides until it bleeds when you press it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it appears red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then press down on the vein from below, until it is raised out of the skin, and then it can be pressed at the joint easily;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut in another place above by three fingers; then scorch the skin over the vein until it appears,
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then ligature the vein, as you have done before, and bind it with another hook, as you did before;
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another vein, or several if needed, then ligature it, and cut the vein in the foot,
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw and ligature it until the second cut; then extract it from cut to cut, until it is all out, then cut it;
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot milk and raise it, then insert an needle tied to a strong double thread,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie it and pull it, and put it under a rod, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out;
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not slip, for if it slips, then one cannot milk or raise it, and it brings harm to the patient;
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have milked it completely, then place on the wound wool moistened with wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	you should split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one covers the vein should be curved, but not cutting, so that it does not cut into the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of a large curve, for if it were thin, it would cut into the vein; but let it be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
De la voinne civile	Of civil bleeding
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This bleeding is restricted to the legs, in warm climates where no herbs or trees grow, and in dry land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	It may also occur elsewhere on the body, and this happens with pustules that form beneath the skin,
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	such as snakes and worms that grow inside the body between the skin and the flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes in the leg,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then change the site, and start the vein coming out, just as a plant's root.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder opens, you must wrap around it a piece of linen from one and a half to two and a half fingers wide, and tie it off,
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen hang down to the leg, and every time it falls away from the body, wind the linen around the body again, and tie it off;
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a portion, and wrap the rest around it, but do not cover the root while it is growing out;
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cover it, it will enter the flesh and cause an abscess and pustules where it is, and a serious illness;
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	for this reason it should be treated little by little until the end, and nothing of it remain in the body;
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this vein, when it is opened, is as long as five or ten palms,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, from whom it grew ten palms in length, and when you cut it off, it bled one drop or opening, and it was perceived all the way to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that all of it came out; and the matter within was evacuated, and in the place were applied healing remedies for several days, then it was cured as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes there are many wounds, and especially when they open at the joints of the feet or on the feet,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and from which much pus flows; treat it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land, because it often happens to oxen:
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	And it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, going up and down all over the body,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it feels like burning as it moves from member to member until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the putrefaction of some humours, such as come up in worms and serpents and roundworms in the belly;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts its maliciousness, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and that happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and bled, one cannot help but wonder what it feels like when it bites:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must tie the area above and below with a strong, tightly bound ligature.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut above and draw it out forcefully, and if the blood is flowing inside the flesh, and you cannot stop it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire until it stops bleeding.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the most harmful things that it does is that it makes the eye water, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the eye, then press underneath it firmly, then grab it and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and one should use a purifying treatment for the body with soluble medicines to eliminate bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of fermenting meats that cause putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	About the pain that comes from flatulence:
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vachair" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then travels from one limb to another; I saw this with my own eyes.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she bared her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of her arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it move up as if it were a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	as quickly as anything, like quicksilver when it moves from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain leaves that area and moves into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later runs through the whole body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it turned around the body, just as I saw her.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never before seen this disease progress in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had seen many who had experienced pain moving from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had not seen it as I did in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because women have soft bodies and uncovered breasts,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and for this reason appears that compulsion of wind.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And it is not apparent according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if the vein above and below is dry, and then apply pressure until that compulsion of wind leaves its place;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the cure is for those who fart wind, as with stinking pills, and serapium pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is such that there are those with large points, small ones, and also flat-headed and hooked.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some have two angles, and some have tongues, and some have pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and those that dislocate in a limb do so in two ways: either in a principal limb they dislocate,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls therefore on any part of these members, and you see the signs of death that I shall tell you hereafter,
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must be careful to extract this arrow, for death follows in many cases.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if you do not see these bad signs and the arrow is not deep inside, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	The sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces the bone and goes through to the brain, and the cerebrospinal fluid leaks out on top of the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is scorching and swelling and blisters and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and loss of senses, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps he loses his senses, or his hearing; and perhaps he loses his speech and voice; and
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is white moisture from the wound, resembling pus, and also blood clots; and
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear, then take care of it, and pull out the arrow if it is not stuck inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the seventh when it falls or turns, are that it is near the left breast, and feels as though it were stuck in a hard object, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the seventh turns just like the pulse, and short black blood comes out, and there is chilliness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without a doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the wound that never leave the chest are foam-filled bile coming from the wound, and a swollen throat, and the patient's colour changing, and high panting, and chilliness leaving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the sole of the foot, it affects the small bones; and causes great swelling and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulder are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance something indigestible might jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the belly, and nothing comes out through the rectum but feces, then there is little hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, and urine comes out and escapes, and the patient feels great pain: know that this wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, forearm, thigh, and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a certain man that an arrow struck him in the cheek or the jaw, at the root of the teeth:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I probed it, and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And draw an arrow through the eye of a needle which has fallen into the fat of the eye below the membrane below.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was re-inserted and could not reach it except for its tip towards the forest,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was as big as an arrow from a Turkish bow, about .i. foot long with a light wooden shaft; the jaw was healed and no bad accident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And draw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab in origin with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved the beards, and I applied subtle remedies until they were cured and the Christians recovered.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I extracted an arrow from a man that was stuck in his belly, and I thought he would die.
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	And then, after thirty days had passed, his condition did not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrowhead, dislodged it, and extracted it, and he experienced no adverse effects.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow lodged in his back, and the wound is sewn up above it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and he does not change his natural habits,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and does not experience any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you wish to treat another man who has an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remain thus without great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And an arrow struck a man of the royal family, the king's nephew, in the eye
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilted to the right; and the arrow was fully inserted
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to attend after she had been struck for 3 days. I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried her with every subtle test, but I didn't feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put on the wound an astringent and digestive poultice, so that the swelling would go down;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and revealed the location of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the ointment again and opened the wound directly, and the patient remained in this state for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow inside his shoulder; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied medicine with a corrosive agent to the wound directly, until it was opened,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I examined it, and felt the tip of the arrow which protruded from the wound;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I applied this medicine to the wound until the head of the arrow became visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it healed well in about four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I lanced the wound that I had pinched with tweezers, and it bled from both sides but could not come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I ceased not to devise and contrive instruments until I made them .i. pair of tongs well made
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what their shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I treated and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And those who have experience judge that cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it therefore, and the wound was sewed up and the patient completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I will now tell you about the extraction of some arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you may apply my advice to those cases which I do not describe, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise doctors understand a little about many things, and about what they know and what they lack,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	they discover new remedies and instruments, and the downward path of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows enter the members where they are stuck according to two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either by the place they enter or by another route;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which goes out by the same place it entered is an arrow entering through fleshy parts, and sometimes it goes out immediately.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not go out immediately, leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes rotten, and relieve the exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it like that for a few days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will pop out, and if it does not, then pierce around the entire nail with a thin needle until the area around the nail is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes all the way to one of the vents of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned are harmful to the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow pierces to the jugular vein it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the jugular vein,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the patient remains for several days without any bad signs, then use the trepan.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is lodged very deeply and cannot be removed, then administer bleeding around the wound, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is lodged within the body where it cannot be seen, then it will go to all parts of the body.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you can feel it, then draw it out with an appropriate instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then open the wound as wide as necessary;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs in the arrowhead so that it holds fast.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can, cut away the flesh that is pierced through by the bone in two places.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or fold back the barbs of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, then leave it until around the nail it becomes soft, then pull it out, for its extraction is easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood makes you feel contrary, then administer what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard against cutting the nerve and the vein, and put on a poultice as you are able to gently pull out the arrow without danger,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, either firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was in when the arrow hit him,
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest help if you can, and if not, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrows that come from another source, or where there is an opening in them, or the skin is swollen and obvious, either seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut away at it with tweezers as much as they can hold, then pull it out; if it will not come out now, leave it.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, rotate your hand around, as far as it goes into the bone, and widen the hole, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then leave it for now, and then try again to extract it until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is an arrowhead, remove the entire arrow;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft is broken, and you see fit to administer a poultice, then apply it with a broad cloth,
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrowhead enters into the wound; and then pull it out,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, put .1 instrument with a pointed end into it to aid in extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrowhead has penetrated, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, as much as you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits in the leg or abdomen or bladder or ribcage, and it is deep, and you can cut above it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard against cutting the vein and nerve, then extract it, then cut the wound if necessary;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to treat arrows is similar to the beak of a bird; see the illustration:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many varieties: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the hair follicle is like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to push out at the tip of an arrow, as the shape shows:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of tweezers for pushing and gripping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common veins of the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one heals are .xxxi., of which it has or head xvi.,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to know: .ij. batants which are after the ears, which are called the two "herbech";
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the  .ij . arteries which are in .ij. temples apparent;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and .ij  veins that are in the .ij  lids of the .ij eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is inside the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called 'augerich'.
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are .v. in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, located on the left side of the neck, and common people call it the "neck vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called the  "fast", and is made up of the cephalic and basilic veins;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it the   "heart vein"; and the basilic vein is located on the right side of the neck,
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the common people "wound of the belly", and it is above the navel,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and is the one that heals, which opens clearly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches:
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot are three veins: one is below the curve of the pouch of the left side,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second sophene which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called 'nesse', which is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are 3 veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old cataracts and with migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bleeding, as I told you, is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then constrict the patient's neck with a rope,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places, depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then grab them with your fingers, and where you feel the pulse underneath your finger, press hard;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance, and stick it under the vein all the way to the bone, then lift your hand up along the vein,
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut through the skin and fascia well .2 times with the knife, and make the blood come out until you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then pull and tie it, so that it heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said about the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the 2 arteries that are in the 2 temples, if it is worth an old emigraine,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and dryness, and habitual blindness, and the body of tears ague to the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and the disease pulls his neck, so that both veins are clearly visible;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels pain in his stomach, and then signs inside;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lightly press the skin above the vein with your thumb, and insert the lance underneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and gently open the vein at the top, and milk it, just as you did with the other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then loosen the bandage, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then place cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their bandaging and extraction, at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as good as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for migraine, and for redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called a "plunger", of which this is the form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And put the tip on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let the blood come out according to the amount you want.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the collar, and ligate the vein until it is healthy and sometimes the work is done with a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too sharp; and ligate the vein crookedly, for the bone is near, and by chance the flames may break when they are delicate.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The ligature of the two veins that are in the two arms helps with thorns, and with tetter, and with ringworm, and with eye-ail, and with facial ailments;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the nature of their ligature is such that the patient should twist his neck in torture by some bond, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then cleanse it, and let the wound be cross-shaped, a little longer than wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are thin, they may break; then stop the bleeding, as much as you need to, and then bind it with a linen bandage, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The wound of the vein of the nose is useful for nosebleed, and for bleeding in the eyes, and for facial diseases,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is chronic;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the healing are such that the patient squeezes his neck, then squeeze his nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	take a long, thin flame and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein will not open well, and the blood will begin to flow now;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it for a night, because it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	it has the shape of a flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The juice of 2 onions helps with the constriction of the windpipe, and with inflammation, and many other illnesses, and with impetigo, and ulcers, and herpes, and stomachaches;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the properties of the juice are such that it pulls the neck out from under both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and the patient lie on his back,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then cleanse the vein from which blood flows profusely, then draw out blood temperately, as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same in another vein, then loosen the ligature, and gently press all the veins,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient is not strangled; and leave it until the morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The salves for sores on the lips above also help with ulcers in the mouth, and gum decay, and lip splits, and inner and outer lips.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the salve is to make the patient sit in front of you, and stretch his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left;
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and distinguish them by their darkness, and by the fact that around them are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	take one from each side; if you do not recognize them and are unsure,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	take the largest from each side, and similarly do the same with the two veins above and below; it is the same procedure.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	On bleeding under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Bleeding the veins under the tongue aids after bleeding the cephalic vein, and it is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and examine the quality of the blood; let the patient hold his tongue out and look underneath each side for a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	examine both, but do not probe too deeply, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm from which blood is commonly drawn are treated in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a very broad needle, an olive-shaped one with a sharp point, called «anesil».;
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and narrow according to the width and tightness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the flame of the myrtle is very famous, and is wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the veins that are smooth, full of thick blood, and contain thick and troubled blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and the shape of the flame is like an olive tree:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed, and is for bleeding the veins gently, where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	Bleeding at the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the bleeder must bleed gently, and be wary of the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he pierces the artery, and there is a gushing of blood, then he must stanch it, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not grip him, but burn him like a torch.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basil does not open clearly, then you must stretch it and change to another;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you may want a vein from him, or you can heal in his place the vein in the arm: it will open clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the flame like a torch, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to find the site of bleeding, you must therefore stretch out the arm and touch it so that you can feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then mark the spot with a sign, then tie up the arm, and then apply the flame cautery.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the spot puffed up, for that is the artery; avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulge upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, then know that it is artery blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	So you therefore hasten and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger when the bleeding stops as often happens.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	hold the arm and leave it thus and not move it until he is healed. And be in fear and not move him until he is better.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and he faints and medicine is not present, then press on the artery above where it is cut and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fir wood, split it, and take one half and bind it on firmly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if he stops bleeding, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said, with powders which stop bleeding.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of bleeding is not difficult in various positions because of the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle helps it to bleed from the top above and the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic vein and the cephalic vein, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to be careful for the nerve that lies beneath, and not to pierce too deeply, and he must find the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and inflames and the nerves are injured, and by chance may not heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens in many people, and if it does not open in some people due to its subtlety, then you should heal it with the instrument gently; and avoid hurting the nerve as much as possible.
