Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is bleeding between the two nerves, they will make a long cut.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The wound of the head, if it bleeds from the scalp, and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to wound with the flame of an olive branch or myrtle, for that is the safest of all veins, as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest place, and not hurt anything if one misses the first time, and one tries again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, some men's parts may become inflamed when one misses the first time, but it does not hurt at all.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only done to maintain health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent illnesses from occurring;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and it should be performed in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first or third day after a wound.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a set time, but when the need arises day or night, at all times and in all weathers.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and one must not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women carrying a fetus from the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	They should not bleed those who are over sixty years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be bled in any way, they should first cleanse the bowels with a gentle enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	If he has retained feces, so that the veins do not attract harmful excess fluids from the intestines to the principal limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor should he bleed those who are too full from meat, nor those who are drunk, as long as they remain so, nor the water-bound;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if one of them has colic after diarrhea, and vomiting, and abdominal discharge, and frequent sexual intercourse, and from exertion, from waking and fasting, and from all that depletes the body, either through weapons or through the body itself;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly withdraw the humors, if the blood is thick, through foods and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then enter the bath, if nothing else weakens him, to subtilize the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and heal the vein around the penis, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and avoid work, strain, and lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be naked and lying down, with the patient above those who are healing him, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then tighten the bandage firmly but not too tightly, for if it is too loose or too tight, it will not work.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the tourniquet with the flame of a little old oil, then place his finger of his left hand on that vein below where he wants to cauterize,
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not bleed and fail when he is cut.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins which flow like cords when cauterized, and some which are filled with winds,
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts it under the flame, it draws back from the flame and cannot open the vein, and so it is with some.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow for this purpose, therefore the surgeon must be skilled in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, try again a little lower at the same site or above it, if the area is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is fearful, leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Perhaps warm pustules will form; do not enter the bath, then restart the bleeding if she wishes.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the orifices are small, then let the blood flow gently and if you doubt that it will not flow as much as you see, then apply direct flame to that orifice itself;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and work on it gently so that the wound is not inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area inflamed, do not restart the bleeding and place a little linseed oil on it, for linseed oil lightens the body of blood and is soothing in this case.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the linseed oil in every bleeding that you open veins, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and it makes a lump and bulge out of them, when one is put in place; so subtly the blood separates and disperses when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there is a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when it has not been lanced before the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you are in a hurry, put a sponge soaked in lukewarm water and salt on the affected area and hold it there for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and you should do this after the blood comes out of the vein, and if it remains in place for several days, there will be no harm;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on it something of aloe or myrrh dissolved in juice of calendula officinalis, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance at the bleeding of basil: place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore placing on it anything of what we have mentioned, for perhaps it cuts into an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its amount and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And one must make a larger wound in a person who is full and bloated, and needs bloodletting, and let the flames be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And one must bleed a weak person in a different way, and they should be bled a little and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is safe from bloodletting and cutting of nerves, and it is better than letting the blood flow long or hard.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And to one whose body needs cleansing, give moistened bread in pomegranate juice; if he is scorched, then draw out blood three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he is of a cold complexion, he should eat moistened bread in sweet wine before the cleansing, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he faints during the cleansing, after the flow of blood, he should inhale the scent of warm broth and subtle, aromatic syrup,
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other remedies we have mentioned in the section on syncope, for opening the veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to wound his arm and bleed again, as needed, when it is weakened by heavy bleeding, let him bleed a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength, continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to wound his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, let him bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is a great deal of blood within the body that has been heated, and it causes fever; therefore one must draw out a large quantity, and widen the orifice so that it drips into a pitcher;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you have inspected all the signs of healing, and place your hand over his pulse when he is healing, so that death does not come upon him from this pain
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this often happens when the healer is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not press hard upon it when you see the arm dislocating and blood issuing out a second time, and the wound is closed,
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked so that he extends his arm suddenly, for this would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let it until it heals the second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that is frozen in the vein comes out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on .a little. piece of salt cloth wetted in vinegar, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be and don't bind it, until the abscess is settled.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to let blood a second time, let it be in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healed in place of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of healing is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the wound turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then let him be bound loosely, so that the vein appears well, then heal it now from the middle, not from the broad or long side;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the slit should be wide, and it should be healed well near the joint of the hand, and if the pus cannot come out, put the hand in hot water again and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not soak the hand in hot water, for one puts it there more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the vein of this vein is saved more from all other veins, that there is no artery or nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the救命 of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Press the hand, and soak it in hot water until the vein is swollen; then release it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it heals crookedly, and if you cut it from all sides, it won't hurt at all;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't go too deep, because the nerves are completely stripped of flesh underneath,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if the pain is frozen in the wound and can't come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have stopped the bleeding as much as necessary, then put oil and silk on the wound to close it quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is useful for the disease of the mice, and do everything as I told you about the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	Bleeding from the ear is useful for all diseases that are beneath the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as well as diseases of the eyes, and retention of fluids, and diseases of the kidneys, and old diseases of the hips, thighs, and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient should put his foot in warm water and rub the wound until it bleeds,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and put it on top of the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot they go a lot of veins;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then tie it on the largest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you tie it on the foot, then be careful of the nerves that are underneath, and tie it across also as though cutting; and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it fails the first time, try again a second time on top of the first cut, for the wound is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt about nerves as we have said, and do likewise to the big toe on the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic nerve is at the back of the leg; its treatment is good for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the nature of its treatment is such that the patient lies on his back and twists upwards at the ankle four times.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is better to leave it as it is, for the place is safe, and it is very painful for many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not treat it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and let the blood flow as much as you want, and then loosen the ligature, and put on cotton and compress it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of bleeding with leeches
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and bleeding is done in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this bleeding without striking is in two ways: either it is all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And bleeding that is done by striking and drawing blood is done in 14 places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	one is at the top of the head, and the other is in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two more on either side of the neck; and the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glasses on the shoulders, and on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cupping glasses in both arms, and in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and suction cups on both ankles; and the cupping does not draw blood except from small veins that are dispersed throughout the body,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore it weakens one no more than bleeding from a vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered, nor with any heat or burning sensation, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, out of necessity or habit, one must be bled, then let it be done every hour at the beginning and end of each month, and throughout all seasons.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are those who, when they need to fart, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and others who experience bloating and redness in their face, head, and neck, and dimness of sight.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and others who spit up a drop of blood, have a swollen tongue, and taste blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are those who dream, and see through the night blood and wounds, and die, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we order him to fast for three hours after daybreak.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	Bleeding from the nose helps with headaches ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this bleeding is in place of the headache,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it should not be used by those of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, because it does them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with serious illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often recover from it become obese, and for this reason, the cupping glasses should be placed a little lower due to the risk of obesity.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Cupping on the neck is in the area of the head and basil, and for this reason, it is useful for the constriction of the feet,
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for splitting of the canal of the lungs, and for coughing, and for congestion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it must be pushed out a little, because if it holds too tightly, it injures the bowels, stomach, and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Ventilation from the two ribs of the neck is good for headache, and eye pain, and brain pain, and strangulation, and tooth root pain,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is in the place of bleeding from the basilic vein; and you must instruct the surgeon to express his hand while placing it so that he does not compress the artery and cause a gush of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation below the chin is good for mouth diseases, and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth a disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The windings of the sides are also worth as much as three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, for the place is naked of flesh and contains nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass which is on the buttock is good for varicose veins and for diseases underneath, and it must be a large cup made of brass, which needs to be applied with great care; and if it were too thin, it would break, causing large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal quickly because they draw blood from throughout the body and are good for old pains in the bones and joints, and the bladder, and restore the flow of fluids; they are located at the sides of the two knees and ankles, and over time they weaken the body and bring about fainting in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is that you first apply it empty, and suck gently, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area become red and swollen, and the blood vessel appear; then release, and re-apply the cupping glasses, and be mindful of the condition of the body, for there are those who have very sensitive skin, and small pores: so one should suck only once, and make wide wounds, and a little deep ones; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, one should suck twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it must be pricked three times; and when we want to draw a little blood, we prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, we prick repeatedly; and if the vein is thick, we pierce it deeply, and the ends are such that the skin is suddenly pierced,
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and for those with thick and tough skin, and who have small pores, you should anoint the places where the leeches will be placed with an astringent and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is on the testicles, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is on the eye, use oil of watercress, or of lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balsam, or aniseed oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one we are healing has soft skin and large pores, then no oil should be used,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but should be washed after fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or pumpkin water, or porcelain water, or similar things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from their bed, or from water of myrrh, and of sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have great excesses arise from old wine, or water of succory, or infusion of aniseed or camomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and one should not bleed with a leech before the bath or enema, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after bleeding,
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it is necessary that he should fast when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who are sick with cholera, and if their blood is too thin and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if they should eat cool things like pomegranates, endive, lettuce with garlic, and similar foods;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink possets, and warm milk, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those with a cold complexion should drink syrup of honey, and mild, aged wine, and warm milk, and possets, and pouters and young birds;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he is bled, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary to give some men triacle or musk before or after bleeding to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and make the drink subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are put on without bleeding are those that are put on the liver, and the mouse, and the podagra, and on the belly and the gut, and the rain, and the hip, because these members do not tolerate bleeding on their eyes,
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and is only done to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we place cups on breasts when they are healthy; to reduce viscosity in the member, as we place cupping jars on the belly and chest to diminish the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it reduces pain, when there is obstruction or stone, and by its attractive power, the obstruction may be removed, or the stone depart from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when placed upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained wind,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with warm water, or with water in which appropriate herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cupping glass administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 inches of width and half a palm of depth, and it has on the side around the middle a small hole, just big enough to push through an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and is of iron, gently applied so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle there is a crossbar of iron or steel, to hold a candle,
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are both large and small according to the illness and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the leeches of children are different from those of the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must thus place this cupping glass upon the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take a candle of wax or a ointment, and place it inside the cupping glass through the tube which is inside the cupping glass,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the flame be at the bottom of the cupping glass so that it does not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it upon the limb, and your fingers must be upon the hole that we have mentioned, so that when one wishes, they can go the vapors, and one removes the cupping glass;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the poultice as before, and reapply it frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the cupping glass which is used for diseases of the lungs, for all kinds of pains, there is neither a rod nor an opening, and it is only applied when it is full of water, and is placed on the affected member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are applied only to small parts of the body where cupping glasses cannot be used due to their size, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and remove their clothing, as with women or children, and others similarly.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the nature of this medicine is such that when you find leeches in clean, fresh water without mud, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in fresh water until they are hungry and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then cleanse the vein and use a cupping glass, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the leeches on top;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are flat and swollen, if it is possible to put a cupping glass on them, then one should, for this is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then raise the part with ease, and then with water, very gently, and then press it out;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the part is too painful after the bite of the snake, then wet .a. linen cloth in cold water and place it over the wound until the swelling is reduced;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the bite is multiple, then place vitriol powder, or gall, and similar things over it until it is reduced;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put raw peas on the area, leaving them until they are cold, and it will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take more leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the leeches will not attach, then wipe the fresh blood from the area, or prick it with a needle until the leech attaches.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them on the area, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will attach.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see them defecate, then powder over a bit of aloe and ground salt, or ash, and they will stop right away.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that the fools mock this chapter, which they have never seen in any ancient book or letter;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason medicine is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and know nothing about it except from the study of ancient books, in which I have delved to acquire knowledge, and through experimentation, and by observing others throughout my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and have summarized it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I have done in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say in the prologue of this book the sums of the words and the chapters where the sage sets his understanding, and remains on truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to someone, you should quickly examine the patient on both sides, if anything holds them back, such as weakness of the body, or children, or the elderly.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the weather is very hot or too cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cool joints, and deer and goat meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have reason to suspect a hot abscess or swelling in the affected limb; then return the patient to their previous treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one should feed the patient foods that promote swelling and粘性, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, feet, pig stomach, offal, fresh fish, and thick wine, and similar things.Et li carnes qui sont de colde norrissement, si conviennent qu’on le fasse manger a grant fin, ou il ait grand besoin; car l’os qui est brisié ne voudroit mie demourer en lieu chaut et colde, s’il le pot eviter.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And meats that are of cold nature should be eaten in moderation, or when there is great need; because a broken bone does not want to stay in a hot and cold place if it can be avoided. For with cool swelling, bruises heal faster.And the meats which are of hot norrissement, si conviennent qu’on le fasse manger en petit quanitite et en grant fin ou il ne se veult mie demourer; car l’os qui est brisié ne voudroit mie demourer en lieu colde et chaut s’il le pot eviter.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the old and the decrepit cannot be well set or healed according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor can those that are too tender, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But do not worry, reset the broken bone with a large tendon that stretches and joins the limb together, so that it enforces as it was before; and do not stop entirely from his work, and for this reason, one should nourish with coarse meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that there are various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter about all types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is one fracture that goes to the bone, and another in sharpening, as with the point of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with a wound, then it is all one small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in each manner, there is its own method and appropriate instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes into its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	For there is known to be the fracture of the bone by what the place is twisted, and it appears well by displacement, and sounds when pressed by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no crookedness nor pain to touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but there may be crookedness, or fissure, or slight fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move it with your hand, but apply remedies that are mentioned below, and then hold it firmly and gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And you should know that fractures that go into the bone, and are the two parts disjoined, they should now be put in an equal point, just as in apatites;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if cold abscesses come, let them alone for a day until the abscesses are soothed;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then put it in the same state as you can easily and gently, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold it steady, as is appropriate hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is in two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or to your hand if it is a small member, or with two strings, or with one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you bring them back together with all your skill and care, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it does not seem right; then set it well, and do not twist or press too hard as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the joint is set, then instruct the patient well not to move it, not while waking or sleeping, not turning or in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and be sure that the joint is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, then it is not at all, and one should put him in such a position that he feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep him straight so that no crookedness comes to him when he is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	Because there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and similar: so you must wrap linen cloth that is soft and thin.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for larger limbs, such as thigh and leg: you must wrap with a wide and firm bandage, because the wide bandages embrace all of the large limb, and constrict it evenly on all sides, so that there is no swelling.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then wind light bandages around it 3 or 4 times depending on the limb, and tighten your hand a little on all of the bandage, then go above the dislocation and tighten less, so that the dislocation is moved away a little.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the bandage a little bit by bit, as long as you press most of the healthy area, then take another bandage and wind it around directly on the dislocated area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part below the fracture, and hold it gently, not too tightly or too loosely, as we said in the first hour above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the ligatures cotton or linen pads so that they are all even, then tie it all with a bandage above, and then put your splints on well, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something hot on the abscess to soothe it, and to reduce the swelling, leave it for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold over your splints, and they should be of a medium-sized cane or of the wood that cleavers are made from, or of palm branches, and they should follow this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary for the star that one puts on the break to be a little larger and broader than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it behooves the member of smallness or greatness;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten on the stars as you did at the first hour, then tie it with a thread similarly, as you did at the first hour over the break;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is, the less it hurts; and the thread should be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft flax;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the threads are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their laces from cords of flax, which is a great error, for the lace cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should not be less than two threads' thickness between each eyelet.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore between the eyes of the stars after the stretching in their healthy state, then place under them linen pads or woolen bandages so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not good to dislocate all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it is not advisable to place splints for more than five or seven days, or longer according to the severity of the hot abscess;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the way of the ancient plaster to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: take flour that is stored on the walls of the mill, and make a paste with plenty of egg, and use this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and it is the common way of the plaster that restores the fracture in many dispositions, especially in women and young children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster to restore fractures, dislocations and twists: take 3 barley grains and ladani and inula and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each 10 grains; aloes, 5 grains; alechil, 8 grains; and make them into powder, and mix them with plenty of egg; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it has a good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and it helps many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that helps with twists: take myrrh and vismalvas, each 10 grains; aloes, 8 grains; açaç, 6 grains; Armenian bole, 10 grains; and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of poultice for joints and bones that have been dislocated from their place, and to soothe the resulting pain, and to reduce swelling: take fresh lamb's skin and soak it in water and cooked oil, and apply it to the affected area. These poultices do not promote healing, but they are good for soothing hot abscesses and reducing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of poultice that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and deadnettle leaves, crush them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of poultice for restoring broken bones and reducing swelling: take the root of the marsh mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, one part each; crush and cook in wine. If the member is inflamed, cook it with moist coriander water or water.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of a stronger poultice than the previous ones, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member: take marsh mallow roots, flax seeds, borage, melilot, and Sansevieria, and violet flowers and chamomile, one part each; crush and cook in water with salt, or sweet water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that one should put on the broken member to restore strength a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and says it should be between two things neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of plaster that helps with injury and pain: take mugwort and shaved human hair, or bird feathers, and bee wax, and mix them together, and make a plaster from it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen it a little later, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor move the bone from its place; if not loosen it by hand every other day.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes in the area, or itching, with restlessness or swelling, then hurry and loosen it and remove the poultice immediately; and take a light cloth and sponge of moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and raise the area, until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on clean linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it up with a bandage, until you are sure that the hot abscess has drained;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then begin again with the subtle binding, and a little poultice, but do not tighten it as much as before; and with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess is reduced and the redness and pain and swelling are gone, then you may need to use poultice and binding again, so begin again as you did before.Et s’il adonques ne se boit li sang, et le membre est sane, si met l’escrivein a la fine de la journee ou au commencement de la nuit;
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb, then do not remove the bandage for three, four, five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and the bone approaches the flesh beneath.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then keep the bandage tighter than before, and increase his food intake, as I said earlier; and if you see the area becoming drier than it should be, know that nourishment cannot reach it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Soak the area in warm water when you remove the bandage, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a little each time.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this action, the nourishment will return to the limb, and reduce the damage caused by the foolishness of those who set the bone crookedly: it is a bad thing, and such work is fearful, and I see nothing else other than causing weariness and doing it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many types of fractures are there, with diverse appearances, and the causes are distinct.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, breaking through to the sinus below the bone, as with a blow from a polearm; this type is called a "polearm fracture."
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts into the bone without breaking through, and this type is called a  "partial fracture;" and the wound of these two fractures are large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a closed fracture, or a split, or from falling on stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if the bone is broken and protruding, reaching the membrane below the bone, or sitting on top of the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is deep in the bone as thin as a hair, and the fracture is small, then this type of fracture is called "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is caused by a stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and the bone is driven inward, and the place is shattered like the potter when they work on pots; then the bone is driven inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have soft bones at the top of their heads, like children's skulls.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens in all these types of fractures that small pieces are dislodged, as I will explain in their own sections.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we should know all types of fractures through examination and observation, and by understanding the corrupt flesh that lies above them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is understood by uncovering the bone and rubbing it with a finger, and if there is a black fracture line.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be aware of adverse events from the injury, and if you see any harmful incidents such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsion, paralysis, fever, eyes bulging out and turning red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then healing is not possible without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see any frightening incidents and expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the child comes to you for the first time and it is winter, then it is necessary to cut the nail before the fourteenth day that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, then you must hurry to cut the nail before the seventh day, otherwise, the tissue underneath the nail will be corrupted and the incidents that we have mentioned will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the split part thus: and it is that you grasp the head of the sick person, and uncover over the bone in all the ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the flow of blood comes to uncover the bone, or the abscess is heated, treat it as it should be, and it is that you fill the place with moistened cloths in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the heated abscess is soothed and you are certain there is no flow of blood; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways: one way is that you cut with a narrow chisel straight ahead, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then insert another chisel larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a variety of different tools, some narrow and some wide, and some pointed, and some made of iron; and work gently so that you do not bleed the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, then you must drill around it, so that you may apply tools with chisels, not so deep as to penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and there should be a rim or ring on top of the point, preventing the point from going beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one fits into its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you may have chisels for every kind of skull; and this is the form of the three kinds of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for drilling around the broken bone is to place one chisel on the bone and turn it with your fingers until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the chisel to another spot a little further, and continue all around; then cut into the space between the holes with incisions, and do this most skillfully and gently, as we have said, until you draw out the bone by hand or with some instrument like tweezers or pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and drawn out the bone, it is fitting that you remove the membrane which is remaining on the bone with any suitable instrument like an incision knife, but it must be more blunt and sharper than the other knives;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if it remains stuck with the small bones or any scales, then loosen them gently with instruments; then treat the wound with poultices and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of operating is that which Galen describes, which is much safer; and he praises it highly, and his word is final.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a portion of the bone where the open fracture is located; then, once that part is uncovered, place under it the tip of this lenticular incision tool, which is shaped thus:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut on one side, but the part that is curved inwards on both sides, so that the cutting edge is towards the bone; then strike it gently with a small mallet, so that you gently chip away at the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane underneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	if it is dislocated at the bone, then the bone must be gently moved, for the bone can be moved without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on top, with small pieces, then one must smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp razor, of which you should have various amounts, in order to use the most suitable one according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take a large razor at first, and then a sharper one, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hairline and subtle fractures, one must apply treatment according to its nature; and this is not a simple task for one who has dedicated their study to this art.
